  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_11813409-3100-4555-86e9-88babdd54092'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer10823678445390634256">No visitors. No nights spent away from the apartment. No disturbing the other residents, all of whom are rich or famous or both. These are the only rules for Jules Larsen's new job as an apartment sitter at the Bartholomew, one of Manhattan's most high-profile and mysterious buildings. Recently heartbroken and just plain broke, Jules is taken in by the splendor of her surr</span>
  <span id="freeText10823678445390634256" style="display:none">No visitors. No nights spent away from the apartment. No disturbing the other residents, all of whom are rich or famous or both. These are the only rules for Jules Larsen's new job as an apartment sitter at the Bartholomew, one of Manhattan's most high-profile and mysterious buildings. Recently heartbroken and just plain broke, Jules is taken in by the splendor of her surroundings and accepts the terms, ready to leave her past life behind.<br /><br />As she gets to know the residents and staff of the Bartholomew, Jules finds herself drawn to fellow apartment sitter Ingrid, who comfortingly, disturbingly reminds her of the sister she lost eight years ago. When Ingrid confides that the Bartholomew is not what it seems and the dark history hidden beneath its gleaming facade is starting to frighten her, Jules brushes it off as a harmless ghost story—until the next day, when Ingrid disappears.<br /><br />Searching for the truth about Ingrid's disappearance, Jules digs deeper into the Bartholomew's dark past and into the secrets kept within its walls. Her discovery that Ingrid is not the first apartment sitter to go missing at the Bartholomew pits Jules against the clock as she races to unmask a killer, expose the building's hidden past, and escape the Bartholomew before her temporary status becomes permanent.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10823678445390634256" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/1615745-just-finished-this-book-and-read-the">Just finished this book and read the “About Author” section at the end of the book. Is the author’s gender intentionally being hidden? I didn’t realize until reading some of the reviews that this was written by a man.</a>
</div>

<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/45284350-laura"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1588699750i/45284350._UX100_CR0,16,100,100_.jpg" /></a>

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/45284350-laura">Laura</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">This was the case for "Final Girls" as well, which is frustrating since I only chose to read it because I thought it was a female author. For folx say<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">This was the case for "Final Girls" as well, which is frustrating since I only chose to read it because I thought it was a female author. For folx saying the author's gender doesn't matter, it absolutely does. I love horror but won't read Stephen King because he can't write a believable character that isn't a white man to save his life. As not-a-white-man, representation and which voice is telling which story means a lot to me. It's even more shameful that Sager made it ambiguous for the reason of sales, when women "do better" than men in so few arenas. I dunno, feels kinda appropriative of sexism issues in the publishing business. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I am a nurse and yes there is an entire team and also they needed to find compatible donors. You don't just find any old person off the street and con<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I am a nurse and yes there is an entire team and also they needed to find compatible donors. You don't just find any old person off the street and conduct an organ transplant! Even though I loved this book it was very well written and the plot and twists were very well done! I tried to get past the last part! He should have done a little better research into that before writing! (Just my opinion!)<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2900169115" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7110082650180005057"><b>Are you f*cking kidding me?!</b><br/><br/>Unpopular opinion below! I originally wrote a long and detailed review discussing all of my issues with this book. However, I don't want to ruin the experience for other readers who might enjoy this book, so I have cut it down to the main points below.<br/><br/><b>The Good</b>: High level of tension and suspense.<br/><br/><b>The Bad</b>: Everything else!<br/><br/><b>Overall</b>: One big convoluted mess. <br/><br/><b>Believability</b>: Nothing is believable. <b>
  <i>NOTHING.</i>
</b><br/><b>The Protagonist: To put it kindly, she is not the brightest bulb. </b></span>
  <span id="freeText7110082650180005057" style="display:none"><b>Are you f*cking kidding me?!</b><br /><br />Unpopular opinion below! I originally wrote a long and detailed review discussing all of my issues with this book. However, I don't want to ruin the experience for other readers who might enjoy this book, so I have cut it down to the main points below.<br /><br /><b>The Good</b>: High level of tension and suspense.<br /><br /><b>The Bad</b>: Everything else!<br /><br /><b>Overall</b>: One big convoluted mess. <br /><br /><b>Believability</b>: Nothing is believable. <b>
  <i>NOTHING.</i>
</b><br /><b>The Protagonist: To put it kindly, she is not the brightest bulb. Yet, she is the one to put the pieces of the mystery together?</b><br /><b>The Mystery</b>: Beyond ridiculous.<br /><b>The narrative:</b> All telling, no seeing.<br /><b>The ending</b>: I have no words.<br /> <br />I tried to dive in and be entertained, but my inner critic would not shut up. I was rolling my eyes so much that it hurt! So much does not add up and I was ready for Jules to die so I wouldn’t have to continue reading about her stupid choices. <b>I am glad this nightmare is over.</b><br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_2578673182" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2578673182" />
    <a title="Chelsea Humphrey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47207032-chelsea-humphrey"><img alt="Chelsea Humphrey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585613513p2/47207032.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2578673182?book_show_action=true">Oct 31, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea Humphrey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea Humphrey" href="/user/show/47207032-chelsea-humphrey">Chelsea Humphrey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781524745141" href="/book/show/42368604-lock-every-door">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Chelsea by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/2925586-dutton">Dutton</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47207032-chelsea-humphrey?shelf=from-publisher">from-publisher</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47207032-chelsea-humphrey?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47207032-chelsea-humphrey?shelf=scared-suspense-reads">scared-suspense-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47207032-chelsea-humphrey?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2578673182" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5556961634037043981"><b>JULY 2019 BOTM SELECTION</b><br/><br/><i>"It certainly doesn't feel cursed. Or haunted. Or any other menacing label you could put on an apartment building. It's comfortable, spacious and, other than the wallpaper, nicely decorated. It's easy to see why Nick and Greta choose to live here. I would certainly stay longer than three months if I could afford to. Which makes it all the stranger that Ingrid chose to leave."</i><br/><br/><b>Muahahahaha.</b> Mr. "Sager" has done it again folks. I'm always wary picking up the forecasted blockb</span>
  <span id="freeText5556961634037043981" style="display:none"><b>JULY 2019 BOTM SELECTION</b><br /><br /><i>"It certainly doesn't feel cursed. Or haunted. Or any other menacing label you could put on an apartment building. It's comfortable, spacious and, other than the wallpaper, nicely decorated. It's easy to see why Nick and Greta choose to live here. I would certainly stay longer than three months if I could afford to. Which makes it all the stranger that Ingrid chose to leave."</i><br /><br /><b>Muahahahaha.</b> Mr. "Sager" has done it again folks. I'm always wary picking up the forecasted blockbusters of the year, but I'll be darned if this isn't his best novel to date, which is saying a lot as I adored <i>The Last Time I Lied</i>. <i>Lock Every Door</i> feels like the author's signature style, but each of his books has a different vibe, in my opinion. <i>Final Girls</i> was horrific slasher, <i>The Last Time I Lied</i> was a campy YA, and <i>Lock Every Door</i> has a grown up, classic chiller feel, with an updated twist on the locked room trope, which is one of my personal favorite plots. Obviously I had high hopes for this book; with a cover that stunning how could you not? <i>And hello, have you read the blurb? Wow!</i> I'm so pleased that I found this to be another winner from the author, and I cannot wait for you to read it as well, friends. <br /><br />I'm not going to give a ton of info about the plot here (tsk tsk), because you want to be surprised, but I will say that I loved the storytelling format used in this book. I'm always game for a countdown, and from the very first page we get a snippet of NOW, followed by a travel backwards in time to a week prior, and from there we are mostly catching back up to the NOW, with a few present tense moments sprinkled between days. This gives the book a growing sense of dread, and what starts as a slow burn quickly turns into a manic frenzy of page turning. <br /><br />This is a plot about missing girls, about status, and about where that privilege can take you. Aside from being a compulsive mystery, and one that I didn't have all figured out before the reveal (happy dance!), <i>Lock Every Door</i> spends a good bit of time investigating grief, loneliness, and how easily we judge those who appear, at first glance, to be a burden on society. I'll stop there, but I really enjoyed and appreciated how the author handled these timely topics and took this story deeper than just an average, pulse-pounding thriller.<br /><br />Eek, I want to say more, but to do so would make me such a bad friend. Do yourself a favor-go in blind, hang on to your butts, and let Sager take you on another devilishly fun thrill ride. If you missed the chance at snagging an early copy via the publisher, please mark this on your summer TBR for July. Purchase it, borrow it from the library, whatever you have to do, just do it! <br /><br /><i>*Many thanks to the publisher for providing my review copy.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="5556961634037043981" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="megs_bookrack" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48328025-megs-bookrack"><img alt="megs_bookrack" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532027727p2/48328025.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2588807332?book_show_action=true">Nov 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="megs_bookrack" class="user" itemprop="url" name="megs_bookrack" href="/user/show/48328025-megs-bookrack">megs_bookrack</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48328025-megs-bookrack?shelf=arcs-read">arcs-read</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2588807332" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer157916892796831916">RILEY SAGER HAS DONE IT <u>AGAIN!!!</u><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1522188843ra/25282489.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>Lock Every Door</i>, follows New Yorker, Jules, who after losing her job and live-in boyfriend all in one day, needs a fresh start. <br/><br/>Forced to crash on her best friend's couch until she can find a place of her own, Jules is beyond desperate to improve her situation.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1472248378ra/20172499.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Determined to get back on her feet, no matter what, Jules discovers an opportunity in a very traditional place, the Classifieds section of a local newspaper.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1459697554ra/18644382.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The post reads: <i>
  <b>Apartment Sitter Wanted.</b>
</i><br/><br/>The Ba</span>
  <span id="freeText157916892796831916" style="display:none">RILEY SAGER HAS DONE IT <u>AGAIN!!!</u><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1522188843ra/25282489.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Lock Every Door</i>, follows New Yorker, Jules, who after losing her job and live-in boyfriend all in one day, needs a fresh start. <br><br>Forced to crash on her best friend's couch until she can find a place of her own, Jules is beyond desperate to improve her situation.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1472248378ra/20172499.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Determined to get back on her feet, no matter what, Jules discovers an opportunity in a very traditional place, the Classifieds section of a local newspaper.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1459697554ra/18644382.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The post reads: <i>
  <b>Apartment Sitter Wanted.</b>
</i><br><br>The Bartholomew is one of the most prestigious apartment buildings in New York City and Jules cannot believe they actually want to interview her for the appointment. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1598321201ra/30011804.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Once inside the building, she is blown away. Honestly, she cannot believe her luck. <br><br>Pristine living quarters, breathtaking views and a handsome guy across the hall, what's not to love?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1448666509ra/17172356.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>In addition to all of those perks, Jules will receive $12,000 to live in the apartment for 3-months. It sounds too good to be true, right? Are there any other requirements? <br><br>Yes, indeed there are, and that's where things start to get sketchy. Jules is told she will not be allowed any visitors, she cannot spend even one night away and she <u>absolutely cannot</u> hassle the other tenants. In fact, any interaction at all is frowned upon.<br><br>Her best friend, Chloe, tries to warn her off, but Jules doesn't see any other options for herself. What choice does she have? This is it.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1563141968ra/27828385.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So, nagging reservations aside, she moves in.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1563141968ra/27828383.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Guys, I freaking loved this book so much. I cannot even describe how much fun this was for me to read. It basically has everything I love. <br><br>Sager's writing sucks you in and the atmosphere is always intense. At this point, it's safe to conclude that I will buy <b>every single book</b> he writes. Ever. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1493650174ra/22638463.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The setting of the Bartholomew was absolutely brilliant. A gothic nightmare in the heart of a bustling city. <br><br>The history surrounding the building, the other tenants, the odd rules; it was all so compelling.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1563141968ra/27828382.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There were scenes, reading late into the night, when I was legit terrified. Without giving anything away, let's just say I have never been so fearful of something as unimposing as a dumbwaiter. <br><br>Ultimately, the plot went in a direction <b>I never would have expected.</b> It was bizarre and so flipping good. This has a <b>real film noir quality to it.</b> Hitchcock, himself, would be impressed.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1563141968ra/27828384.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This was my <u>most anticipated thriller of 2019</u> and it did not disappoint for a moment. I loved every minute of reading <i>Lock Every Door</i>!<br><br>Thank you <u>so much</u>, PENGUIN GROUP Dutton, for providing me with a copy to read and review. I cannot even express my level of gratitude.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1599939063ra/30098111.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_3581100474" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3581100474" />
    <a title="Cindy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57797254-cindy"><img alt="Cindy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598112512p2/57797254.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3581100474?book_show_action=true">Oct 08, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cindy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cindy" href="/user/show/57797254-cindy">Cindy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3581100474" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8289206405556650268">I was engaged while listening to this book; it's an easy and simple read that helps as a palate cleanser in-between more dense stories. I found this thriller to be too slow for my tastes though, and since I was able to predict several things that were revealed, the slow burn ended up not having much payoff for me. There's potential for a deeper exploration of classism and financial inequality, but it's very on-the-nose to the point where the antagonists become cartoonish.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2656064473" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2656064473" />
    <a title="j e w e l s" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68216634-j-e-w-e-l-s"><img alt="j e w e l s" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1552606306p2/68216634.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2656064473?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="j e w e l s" class="user" itemprop="url" name="j e w e l s" href="/user/show/68216634-j-e-w-e-l-s">j e w e l s</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68216634-j-e-w-e-l-s?shelf=recent-faves">recent-faves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68216634-j-e-w-e-l-s?shelf=books-bejeweled">books-bejeweled</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2656064473" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1573852660196827944"><b>FIVE STARS IT'S HERE IT'S HERE!!!!</b><br/><a href='https://fontmeme.com/game-of-thrones-font/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1558923207i/27576666._SX540_.png' alt='game-of-thrones-font' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a>You know what that means, don’t you?<br/><br/>Writer <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/15263414.Riley_Sager' title='Riley Sager' rel='nofollow noopener'>Riley Sager</a><b> OWNS</b> July. For the third year in a row, Sager is set to drop another stunning thriller in July. As a die-hard Sager fan, I’m here to tell you it may just be his best yet! <b>MERRY CHRISTMAS TO YOU. IN JULY.</b>🎄<br/><br/>I don’t know how Riley Sager does it. Every book is better than his last! <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41837243.Lock_Every_Door' title='Lock Every Door by Riley Sager' rel='nofollow noopener'>Lock Every Door</a> is buttoned up tight and in ship shape, spic-n-span order for your thrilling pleasure!<br/><br/>As in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32796253.Final_Girls' title='Final Girls by Riley Sager' rel='nofollow noopener'>Final Girls</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36626748.The_Last_Time_I_Lied' title='The Last Time I Lied by Riley Sager' rel='nofollow noopener'>The L</a></span>
  <span id="freeText1573852660196827944" style="display:none"><b>FIVE STARS IT'S HERE IT'S HERE!!!!</b><br><a href="https://fontmeme.com/game-of-thrones-font/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1558923207i/27576666._SX540_.png" alt="game-of-thrones-font" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a>You know what that means, don’t you?<br><br>Writer <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/15263414.Riley_Sager" title="Riley Sager" rel="nofollow noopener">Riley Sager</a><b> OWNS</b> July. For the third year in a row, Sager is set to drop another stunning thriller in July. As a die-hard Sager fan, I’m here to tell you it may just be his best yet! <b>MERRY CHRISTMAS TO YOU. IN JULY.</b>🎄<br><br>I don’t know how Riley Sager does it. Every book is better than his last! <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41837243.Lock_Every_Door" title="Lock Every Door by Riley Sager" rel="nofollow noopener">Lock Every Door</a> is buttoned up tight and in ship shape, spic-n-span order for your thrilling pleasure!<br><br>As in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32796253.Final_Girls" title="Final Girls by Riley Sager" rel="nofollow noopener">Final Girls</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36626748.The_Last_Time_I_Lied" title="The Last Time I Lied by Riley Sager" rel="nofollow noopener">The Last Time I Lied</a>, we have a lovable heroine trying to get out of the jam of a lifetime. You will be rooting Jules on as she tries like crazy to figure out what thaaaaaa hellllll is going on. First thing in the story, she answers a Craigslist ad to work as an apartment sitter in the exclusive Bartholemew building right across from Central Park in NYC. She is to be paid $1000 per week to live in this gorgeous Gothic building. Just as long as she follows a few simple rules. <b>YIKES</b>. The rules are a bit strict, but our Jules is desperate for moolah and feels she’s got nothin to lose. Sooooooo…..Oh, boy. <br><br>She should’ve paid attention to those rules! Just like a roach motel, those who enter The Bartholomew never leave The Bartholomew. <br><br>The premise reminds me of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/39863515.An_Anonymous_Girl" title="An Anonymous Girl by Greer Hendricks" rel="nofollow noopener">An Anonymous Girl</a>, but Sager has a style all his own. He manages to keep the tone light and fun, almost Scooby doo-like, with all the “kids” out to solve a crime in their Mystery Machine Van. I really enjoy this aspect! <br><br>It is a creepy and addictive read. As usual, Sager approaches the “over-the-top” believability factor, but, for some reason, with Sager, you just let it slide. It is so much more fun just to go along with him! I love the NYC setting and the characters to root for. Of course, a satisfying ending for us! All in all, a fantastic beach read!<br><br><i>Thanks very much to Netgalley for letting me read and review the advance copy. This is my REAL OPINION!</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="1573852660196827944" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2579394532" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1855735081480497170"><em>
  <strong>Is it over-the-top craziness?.... yep</strong>
</em><br/><br/><em>
  <strong>Is it addictive and entertaining?... absolutely!</strong>
</em><br/><br/><em>
  <strong>Did I feel like I was right next to Jules with my heart-pounding along with her?.... I was practically holding her hand!</strong>
</em><br/><br/>Who is Jules, you might ask? She is the ever so curious protagonist who becomes an amateur sleuth when her stay at the ever so famous <strong>Bartholomew Apartment </strong>building begins to uncover its unsettling past. The buildings deep, dark secrets begin to surface, bubbling over. It's Gothic s</span>
  <span id="freeText1855735081480497170" style="display:none"><em>
  <strong>Is it over-the-top craziness?.... yep</strong>
</em><br /><br /><em>
  <strong>Is it addictive and entertaining?... absolutely!</strong>
</em><br /><br /><em>
  <strong>Did I feel like I was right next to Jules with my heart-pounding along with her?.... I was practically holding her hand!</strong>
</em><br /><br />Who is Jules, you might ask? She is the ever so curious protagonist who becomes an amateur sleuth when her stay at the ever so famous <strong>Bartholomew Apartment </strong>building begins to uncover its unsettling past. The buildings deep, dark secrets begin to surface, bubbling over. It's Gothic structure is over a hundred-years old and some disturbing articles have been written about it.<br /><br />Could she have made a mistake choosing to live here? The Gargoyle outside her window stood tall and ominous.  It didn't creep Jules out though, she thought it was like "<em>a protector standing guard</em>."  She doesn't realize it quite yet, but she will need a protector!<br /><br />I was completely drawn into this highly entertaining and unpredictable tale of the Bartholomew's dark past with its observing walls and quirky, wealthy residents. I just had to find out what happened to the other missing apartment sitters.<br /><br /><strong>I DARE NOT</strong> say more.... just read it for yourself and you can hold Jules hand as she tries to plan her escape!<br /><br />Buddy read - Thanks for entertaining me with all your wild predictions along the way Kendall! Of course none of them were as wild as what actually happened!!<br /><br />This one is sure to stir up some discussions! Don't miss it. OUT on July 2,2019.<br /><br />Thanks to the publisher / NG for my copy to review.<br /><br /> </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2656281729" />
    <a title="Gabby" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26560207-gabby"><img alt="Gabby" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1482222518p2/26560207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2656281729?book_show_action=true">Jul 02, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gabby" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gabby" href="/user/show/26560207-gabby">Gabby</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26560207-gabby?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26560207-gabby?shelf=botm">botm</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26560207-gabby?shelf=love-the-concept">love-the-concept</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26560207-gabby?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26560207-gabby?shelf=read-in-one-day">read-in-one-day</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26560207-gabby?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26560207-gabby?shelf=read-in-2019">read-in-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26560207-gabby?shelf=thrillers-or-mystery">thrillers-or-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26560207-gabby?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26560207-gabby?shelf=liked-it">liked-it</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2656281729" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18190367797832313232"><b>Holy shit this book was intense and creepy.</b> This is my third time reading a thriller from Riley Sager, and wow this book is great, it's my new favorite.<br/><br/>This story follows this girl Jules who is desperate for a job when she stumbles upon this too good to be true opportunity to live in this glamorous apartment building in New York and they will pay her to be a tenant there. Except for the building is said to be cursed / haunted / shady. But she desperately needs the money and she’s always wanted t</span>
  <span id="freeText18190367797832313232" style="display:none"><b>Holy shit this book was intense and creepy.</b> This is my third time reading a thriller from Riley Sager, and wow this book is great, it's my new favorite.<br /><br />This story follows this girl Jules who is desperate for a job when she stumbles upon this too good to be true opportunity to live in this glamorous apartment building in New York and they will pay her to be a tenant there. Except for the building is said to be cursed / haunted / shady. But she desperately needs the money and she’s always wanted to live there since she was a little girl so it seems like a win/win situation. Until it’s not.<br /><br /><b>This book was creepy</b> and it felt like a perfect mix of thriller of horror, which is something I love about all of Riley Sager’s books. They always have this haunting atmosphere and feel slightly paranormal or creepy, like someone is always watching the main character and I eat that shit up, I love it!!! <br /><br />There were some truly creepy moments in this book that gave me chills?? I felt like I was in the apartment building because the descriptions were so vivid. Even though this is a typical “girl goes missing” thriller and we spend the majority of the book trying to figure out what happens to this girl, it was still so much more than that and it was such a fun but also disturbing read. The ending got a lot more dark than I was expecting it to.<br /><br />I really enjoyed this book so much and if you’re a fan of thrillers with a touch of horror I highly recommend this! 🤗 I reread this book as an audiobook and it was just as fun to listen to, I enjoyed it so much.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18190367797832313232" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2778998557" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2778998557" />
    <a title="Nilufer Ozmekik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53701594-nilufer-ozmekik"><img alt="Nilufer Ozmekik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559807601p2/53701594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2778998557?book_show_action=true">Jul 09, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nilufer Ozmekik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nilufer Ozmekik" href="/user/show/53701594-nilufer-ozmekik">Nilufer Ozmekik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781524745141" href="/book/show/42368604-lock-every-door">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2778998557" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5752692885880625765">Three lalalaa here comes unpopular review alarm, I can hear the ominous soundtrack in my head like Jaws’s approaching, nanana, disappointing, I got so excited, cleared my night to date with this book, but I didn’t like what I got at the end and my husband laughs at me when he is binge watching Stranger Things( at least one of us is happy) stars!!!<br/><br/> Oh boy, I usually love Riley Sager’s writing style. I enjoyed “ Final Girls” and literally devoured “Last time I lied” ( as soon as I finished I got m</span>
  <span id="freeText5752692885880625765" style="display:none">Three lalalaa here comes unpopular review alarm, I can hear the ominous soundtrack in my head like Jaws’s approaching, nanana, disappointing, I got so excited, cleared my night to date with this book, but I didn’t like what I got at the end and my husband laughs at me when he is binge watching Stranger Things( at least one of us is happy) stars!!!<br /><br /> Oh boy, I usually love Riley Sager’s writing style. I enjoyed “ Final Girls” and literally devoured “Last time I lied” ( as soon as I finished I got my stomach pumped to get rid of eaten pages  )<br /><br /> I still enjoyed the writing and characterization of heroine, Jules ( not my favorite name choice but I shouldn’t judge a person from her or his unpopular name) a real survivor, suffering from two big tragedies in her life ( losing her parents in a fire and her missing sister who might be kidnapped or killed), jobless, penniless, homeless after being cheated by her scumbag boyfriend and left his place. <br /><br />You may feel like she’s damaged, she’s fragile, broken but not exactly! She’s brave (She saved an snob best seller writer and a cute dog from fire by putting her life at risk) fast thinker to stay afloat on water ( She accepts her new job as apartment sitter at the Bartholomew which is a real spooky place with the deaths from Spanish flu to suicide and murder.), so determined to find the truth about Ingrid who is also missing, reminds Jules of her sister, at the risk of losing her place at the apartment and violating her contract rules.<br /><br />This book’s story development and a little part of the ending have quiet resemblances with “Rosemary’s baby”! At least the apartment management doesn’t hire young people to have sex with devil and have beautiful satanic children looking like Tom Ellis. <br />It also reminded me of TV series named “666 Park Avenue”( as you see the door number you may imagine what is about and as you see the cancellation after 13 episodes, this concept also didn’t work for TV, too. )<br /><br />THE THINGS I LIKED: Heroine Jules, her fighting and surviving instincts, the slow beginning of story ( it might be called slow-burn thriller, but at the end thriller part burned itself ) which gives you goosebumps, quiet shivering, hooked you from the beginning and turning the pages faster as you can( be careful not to have paper cuts).<br /><br />WHAT I DIDN’T LIKE: As soon as I read the revelation part which is not something so supernatural or satanic by the way, seemed like a little easy way out for me! Maybe I was waiting for more surprises, more twisty, edgy, terrifying, unforeseeable results. Because at the previous books of the author, I got all of them. But on this one, the ending was a little soft and regular. It didn’t shake me to my core( Lately several thriller books I read gave me this feeling maybe my pain threshold is in the maximum point so I want to read something more challenging!)<br /><br />So beginning is great, middle of the still good but ending ERRRRRR: You gave the wrong answer and you disqualified! <br /><br />As a summary, this book is above the average, descriptions, character analysis and development are well crafted, you may easily relate with the poor apartment sitters and their tragic lives. But I expected more from the author because of his brilliant past works. So thanks but no thanks, this is not my book, not my cup of tea( I only drink black coffee)! Let’s move to the other new releases!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5752692885880625765" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Debra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5032725-debra"><img alt="Debra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1525132364p2/5032725.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2579302489?book_show_action=true">Jul 07, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Debra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Debra" href="/user/show/5032725-debra">Debra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5032725-debra?shelf=traveling-frends-summer-reading-cha">traveling-frends-summer-reading-cha</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2579302489" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10428402380951670459">Rules, Rules, Rules- YOU MUST OBEY THE RULES. They are simple rules really - do not disturb the other residents at the Bartholomew, no overnight visitors and you must spend every night in your apartment. With added questions thrown in about drinking, smoking, family, etc.<br/><br/>Reeling from a recent breakup, Jules has been sleeping on her best friend’s couch, when she sees the ad for an apartment sitter on Craigslist, she applies for the job. After answering some background questions, she is hired as a</span>
  <span id="freeText10428402380951670459" style="display:none">Rules, Rules, Rules- YOU MUST OBEY THE RULES. They are simple rules really - do not disturb the other residents at the Bartholomew, no overnight visitors and you must spend every night in your apartment. With added questions thrown in about drinking, smoking, family, etc.<br /><br />Reeling from a recent breakup, Jules has been sleeping on her best friend’s couch, when she sees the ad for an apartment sitter on Craigslist, she applies for the job. After answering some background questions, she is hired as and can't believe her luck, getting paid a lot of money to live in such a beautiful and grand building. She shrugs off her best friends doubts and concerns and moves and makes friends with another apartment sitter named Ingrid. Who cares about the building’s creepy history, money is money, right? But soon Jules begins to hear strange noises at night and Ingrid alludes to the fact that the Bartholomew may not be what it seems...and then Ingrid goes missing. Ever hear the adage "If it seems too good to be true, it usually is." My first thought was why would a building which houses celebrities and wealthy people advertise on craigslist and not some ritzy house-sitting company????? Hmm…. now I know! While searching for her missing friend, Jules begins to learn more about the Bartholomew and its dark history. <br /><br />I was fully engaged in this book and found it to have moments of dread and suspense. He piqued my curiosity right away and held it for most of the book. This became a real page turner for me. I had several theories and guesses about what was going to happen and I did not see that ending coming. I'll be honest, the ending was a little bit of a letdown for me. Having said that, I still found this to be a fast read which sucked me in and kept my attention. <br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10428402380951670459" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer3113756700" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer7169909964112855369">what i really appreciate about RSs writing is he knows how to create a thrilling story without inducing nightmares as a side-effect. i will totally own up to be a massive wimp, so i like the opportunity of being able to read a spooky story without my over-active imagination getting the best of me. <br/><br/>and although this didnt scare me, i did quietly whisper <i>‘what the heck?!’</i> so many times throughout this. i mean, the last third is so, so, so bizarre. thrilling, but bizarre. i dont even know how RS ca</span>
  <span id="freeText7169909964112855369" style="display:none">what i really appreciate about RSs writing is he knows how to create a thrilling story without inducing nightmares as a side-effect. i will totally own up to be a massive wimp, so i like the opportunity of being able to read a spooky story without my over-active imagination getting the best of me. <br /><br />and although this didnt scare me, i did quietly whisper <i>‘what the heck?!’</i> so many times throughout this. i mean, the last third is so, so, so bizarre. thrilling, but bizarre. i dont even know how RS came up with the idea because its totally out in left field. but it really worked with the mood and atmosphere of the story. <br /><br />this was a lot of fun to read and cant wait to pick up the next RS book!<br /><br /><b>↠ <i>3.5 stars</i></b></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11055337680597431301">Ho. Lee. Chit.<br/><br/>What a page-turner. I found myself awake until the sun came up, frantically turning the pages to get to the end because ...<br/><br/>I COULDN'T WAIT FOR IT TO BE OVER!!<br/><br/>I LOOOOOVED Final Girls. That may be because I have a special connection to it that I'm positive nobody cares about but either way, I thought it was superb.<br/><br/>I LIKED The Last Time I Lied. <br/><br/>I LOATHED everytime I had to pick up Lock Every Door.<br/><br/>Much like Sager's previous works, this is a slow burn, taking it's time leading you to a </span>
  <span id="freeText11055337680597431301" style="display:none">Ho. Lee. Chit.<br /><br />What a page-turner. I found myself awake until the sun came up, frantically turning the pages to get to the end because ...<br /><br />I COULDN'T WAIT FOR IT TO BE OVER!!<br /><br />I LOOOOOVED Final Girls. That may be because I have a special connection to it that I'm positive nobody cares about but either way, I thought it was superb.<br /><br />I LIKED The Last Time I Lied. <br /><br />I LOATHED everytime I had to pick up Lock Every Door.<br /><br />Much like Sager's previous works, this is a slow burn, taking it's time leading you to a combustible conclusion. This ending, however, didn't even singe my eyebrows.<br /><br />The characters, especially the main character, are annoying and unrealistic.<br /><br />This book has no idea what it wants to be. Is it a ghost story? A murder mystery? By the end, did I even care? No. No I didn't. <br /><br />The ending twist is contrived at best. <br /><br />I can't even tell you why the author chose the title. <br /><br />2 ⭐⭐ because, well, I don't really know. <br /><br /><br />*** I was provided an ARC copy from Penguin-Random House First to Read program in exchange for an honest review. *** <br /><br />P.S. this program is closing down in June and I want to cry although after this review I doubt they'd ever give me another ARC.</span>

<div id="review_2872504255" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2872504255" />
    <a title="Barbie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/90413527-barbie"><img alt="Barbie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601722083p2/90413527.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2872504255?book_show_action=true">Jun 26, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Barbie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Barbie" href="/user/show/90413527-barbie">Barbie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2872504255" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15591909068537458435"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1551534793i/27143282._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b> My thoughts in a nutshell </b><br/>I had high hopes for this one, and it doesn't live up to my expectation. I'm not saying that it was a bad book, but it isn't a 5 stars read like his other book (<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36626748.The_Last_Time_I_Lied' title='The Last Time I Lied by Riley Sager' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Last Time I Lied</a>). I still like it.<br/><br/><b>The story is about…</b><br/><u>Skip over this point if you don't like the sneak peek. </u><br/>... an old apartment where strange things start to happen. <br/>No visitors. Too strict rules. People have gone missing. It is a nightmare. <br/>Jules Larsen's new job is in here. She will be an apartment sitt</span>
  <span id="freeText15591909068537458435" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1551534793i/27143282._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b> My thoughts in a nutshell </b><br>I had high hopes for this one, and it doesn't live up to my expectation. I'm not saying that it was a bad book, but it isn't a 5 stars read like his other book (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36626748.The_Last_Time_I_Lied" title="The Last Time I Lied by Riley Sager" rel="nofollow noopener">The Last Time I Lied</a>). I still like it.<br><br><b>The story is about…</b><br><u>Skip over this point if you don't like the sneak peek. </u><br>... an old apartment where strange things start to happen. <br>No visitors. Too strict rules. People have gone missing. It is a nightmare. <br>Jules Larsen's new job is in here. She will be an apartment sitter. What will happen to her? Nobody knows.<br><br><b> What impressed me </b><br>Lock Every Door is a slow-paced novel. I adored the slow build-up situation because it gave me enough tension and I couldn't put it down.<br><blockquote>
  <i>Every so often, life offers you a reset button. When it does, you need to press it as hard as you can. </i>
</blockquote><br>My favorite impression of the book was the old apartment atmosphere. It was intense and creepy. I felt like I was there but I don't want to be there, in a spooky, old house. <br><blockquote>
  <i>Never take anything you haven't earned, my father used to say. You always end up paying for it one way or another. </i>
</blockquote><br>I admire the two-time line idea. It was so good when the two lines meet and things turn out.<br>All of the characters were fucked up. In the first half of the book, I knew who the "villain" is. It wasn't a surprise to me, but I didn't know what was going to happen.<br><blockquote>
  <i>One time is an anomaly. Two times is a coincidence. Three times is proof.</i>
</blockquote><br>I'm relieved because Sager does not choose that plot twist. If you have read it, you know what I mean. <br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br>I think the satanic/sect twist. I don't like that part. I can't enjoy a story about exorcism or something like that. Maybe I haven't find the right one yet. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>So, the final solution was excellent! It is so disturbing for me. I can read a book about gory or gruesome parts without me feeling sick, but there is one thing that makes me uncomfortable.<br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br>Illegal organ transplant. When somebody is kidnapped and his/her organs are taken. In the book, the doctor told Jules that her kidney, heart, and liver gets another patient. I can't handle it. It is so horrible and disgusting. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>The writing style was captivating. Riley Sager is a brilliant thriller expert. He knows how to maintain stress.<br><br><b>What I don't like </b><br>I don't connect to the main protagonist Jules. She was so dumb sometimes and I don't really understand what her motive was. Why does she do stupid things? Okay, she was broke. In my opinion, money is not as important as her life. I hate this cliché when the character sacrifices his/her life because they don't have enough cash. WTF? Why is it better? She will be dead, and that's all about her money. Soooo sooo feeble-minded.<br>There was some occasion that were hard to believe or just superficial. <br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The phone was hacked in 5 minutes.<br>The people from Bartholomew wants Jules to find Ingrid, but they stop her. It doesn't make any sense.<br>Jules' sister disappeared in the past, but we have absolutely no idea what happened to her. It was unnecessary.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b> Make a conclusion </b><br>Overall, it will be a divisive novel because it is slow, and the twist won't work for everyone. <br>I gave it 4 stars. I like the gothic mood, and I couldn't put it down. It was a great page-turner. <br><b> I say that if you like a slow-moving but very atmospheric thriller, I highly recommend it. </b> I don't think it was a horror. I didn't feel any fear.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="15591909068537458435" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2790203254" />
    <a title="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin"><img alt="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603831478p2/17438949.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2790203254?book_show_action=true">Sep 07, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" href="/user/show/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin">Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2849737566" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16812350676510275735"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1562178019i/27762052._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i>ARC acquired at <a href='https://youtu.be/27bxzSm9lq8' rel='nofollow noopener'>Book Expo</a> in exchange for an honest review.</i><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“The twelfth floor is special”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><i>Lock Every Door</i> is about a girl name Jules, who wakes up in a hospital after being hit by a car. She is twenty-five, recently single, and very much struggling with money. But then she gets an opportunity to apartment sit in a very rich and exclusive complex in Manhattan. <br/><br/>All of the floors in the apartment complex have four units, except for the twelfth floor, which only has two, and one of those </span>
  <span id="freeText16812350676510275735" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1562178019i/27762052._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>ARC acquired at <a href="https://youtu.be/27bxzSm9lq8" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Expo</a> in exchange for an honest review.</i><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“The twelfth floor is special”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><i>Lock Every Door</i> is about a girl name Jules, who wakes up in a hospital after being hit by a car. She is twenty-five, recently single, and very much struggling with money. But then she gets an opportunity to apartment sit in a very rich and exclusive complex in Manhattan. <br><br>All of the floors in the apartment complex have four units, except for the twelfth floor, which only has two, and one of those units happen to be the one that needs apartment sitting. Basically, our main character, Jules, will earn 4,000 a month, for three months, but no one is allowed in the apartment besides herself, and she is also expected to not get close to any of the other tenants, since they are mostly high profile celebrities who value their privacy. <br><br>Jules accepts, without question, even though the secrecy does give her a strange vibe. The new endeavor also takes a strange twist when the author of the book that she and her sister (who has been missing for almost a decade) obsessed over, <i>Heart of the Dreamer</i>, lives in the apartment complex. But Jules quickly befriends a couple other apartment sitters, who seem to know more information about this too good to be true offer they have all accepted. <br><br>You quickly meet many of the residents of this apartment, but when one goes missing, you will start to question it all, right along side Jules. And my favorite part of this story, was getting to know all of the players in this game and trying to piece together their probable motives. And honestly? I really loved reading the twists and turns, right up until the very end, sadly. <br><br>I didn’t like the end of this book, which I feel like is a <i>very</i> unpopular opinion. I just feel like it took a lot of inspiration from a <i>very</i> famous, award winning movie. I can’t tell you which movie, without completely spoiling the twist, but it was just too apparent for my liking and honestly just really ruined the ending for me. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[it’s <a href="https://www.imdb.com/title/tt5052448/" rel="nofollow noopener">Get Out</a>  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Overall, this was a fun reading experience for the most part. This was my second book by the author, and I feel like he has a very captivating writing style that not only keeps you on your toes with guessing, but makes it almost impossible to not read his book in one sitting, because you never want to put it down. <br><br><a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.twitter.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://meltotheany.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC4RbHEg_fH6CewJrh_0xJ9g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitch</a><br><br><b>Content and Trigger Warnings:</b> talk of being cheated on in the past, talk of loss of a loved one in the past, self-harm (fire + hand), talk of past suicide, talk of cancer, and murder. <br><br><b>[EXTRA:]</b> Holy moly, <a href="https://deadline.com/2019/07/lock-every-door-series-based-on-novel-in-works-at-paramount-tv-anonymous-content-with-true-blood-duo-1202640999/" rel="nofollow noopener"><i>Lock Every Door</i> is going to be adapted</a>! <br><br>Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/42754031-becky-coffeecocktailsandbooks" rel="nofollow noopener">Becky</a> &amp; <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/29682167-madison-mary" rel="nofollow noopener">Madison Mary</a>! ❤</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="16812350676510275735" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2797773332" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2797773332" />
    <a title="Matthew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16254355-matthew"><img alt="Matthew" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464987365p2/16254355.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2797773332?book_show_action=true">Oct 30, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matthew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matthew" href="/user/show/16254355-matthew">Matthew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781984891068" href="/book/show/46147591-lock-every-door">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of creepy, mysterious thrillers with a twist</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=2019">2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=suspense">suspense</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2797773332" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7877085698786736185">This has been, by far, my favorite Riley Sager book so far!<br/><br/>While some of the plot ended up being familiar from other stories I have seen/read, that is pretty normal for most books. Throughout novels these days, there are lot of retellings of similar plots lines, it just depends on how you tell it. In the case of this particular thrilling and creepy plot twist, I was quite impressed.<br/><br/>If I could sum up why this is a 5-star book in 1 sentence: <b>
  <u>I could not stop for the last 1/5 of this book. </u>
</b> <br/><br/>COU</span>
  <span id="freeText7877085698786736185" style="display:none">This has been, by far, my favorite Riley Sager book so far!<br /><br />While some of the plot ended up being familiar from other stories I have seen/read, that is pretty normal for most books. Throughout novels these days, there are lot of retellings of similar plots lines, it just depends on how you tell it. In the case of this particular thrilling and creepy plot twist, I was quite impressed.<br /><br />If I could sum up why this is a 5-star book in 1 sentence: <b>
  <u>I could not stop for the last 1/5 of this book. </u>
</b> <br /><br />COULD NOT STOP! I was riveted by the climax and resolution of this book. It is the most riveted I have been in a long time! Whether there we any other negatives to detract from my review of this book (and there really were not), the end was enough to make up for anything else.<br /><br />The book was suspenseful, creepy, thrilling, and mysterious. Great characters with plenty of development in what was a relatively short book. And, as mentioned above, I loved the ending and I DID NOT SEE IT COMING! My guesses were not even close. I love a book where when you finally get to the resolution, you are like “OH DANG!”<br /><br />I highly recommend this to all who love creepy, twisted mysteries – I don’t think you will be disappointed!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7877085698786736185" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3372183540191552879">Just when I’d given up hope on finding a fun summer thriller, along comes this book! <br/><br/>Jules is having a string of bad luck and finds herself without a home and job, little money in her bank account, and no family to lean on for support. She answers an ad for an apartment sitter at The Bartholomew, an exclusive luxurious apartment building in NYC. The pay to stay in this fancy apartment? $1K a week. She can’t believe her stroke of good luck when she is hired. Apparently Jules forgot the adage that</span>
  <span id="freeText3372183540191552879" style="display:none">Just when I’d given up hope on finding a fun summer thriller, along comes this book! <br /><br />Jules is having a string of bad luck and finds herself without a home and job, little money in her bank account, and no family to lean on for support. She answers an ad for an apartment sitter at The Bartholomew, an exclusive luxurious apartment building in NYC. The pay to stay in this fancy apartment? $1K a week. She can’t believe her stroke of good luck when she is hired. Apparently Jules forgot the adage that if it sounds too good to be true, it is too good to be true.<br /><br />There are a few rules: no visitors, no nights away from the apartment, no talking to or otherwise bothering the wealthy residents, and no posts on social media. Desperate for money, Jules agrees.<br /><br />Soon, she begins hearing strange noises and tales of mysterious deaths and hauntings. When an apartment sitter Jules befriends goes missing, she discovers this wasn’t the first sitter to mysteriously disappear, and she goes in search for answers. Answers that turn out to be far more sinister than she could have imagined.<br /><br />This is a Riley Sager book, so It’s not a spoiler to say there are twists and turns in this creepy, gothic suspense tale where the Bartholomew becomes a character itself. The palpable sense of eeriness with Jules all alone in the world up against some creepy neighbors in a gothic apartment building gave me a Rosemary’s Baby vibe.<br /><br />Jules is a strong, relatable, and engaging character. The toggling between past and present builds the tension to a fever pitch. I listened to the audiobook and the narrator was excellent. It was so engaging that I listened to the entire book in 2 days. Love it or hate it, I didn’t see the end coming, and it blew me away <br /><br />I wasn’t a huge fan of the author’s first two books but after seeing glowing reviews for this book from readers who felt the same way, I took a chance and I’m so glad I did. This was a buddy read with Marialyce and one we both loved. Highly recommended for fans of gothic suspense.<br /><br />For our duo review of this and other books please visit <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://yayareadslotsofbooks.wordpress.com">https://yayareadslotsofbooks.wordpres...</a></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4165512109041565596">Jules Larsen is down on her luck. She just lost her job and her boyfriend all in one day. Now, with no new jobs on the horizon, staying on her friends couch may be more permanent than she anticipated.<br/><br/>That is, until the opportunity of a lifetime falls into her lap! Stay at the Bartholomew apartment building in New York City. One of the most famous landmarks with a dark, mysterious history behind it. And…She’ll be paid twelve thousand dollars to apartment sit! <b>Seriously! How could she say no!?</b><br/><br/>Ahhh</span>
  <span id="freeText4165512109041565596" style="display:none">Jules Larsen is down on her luck. She just lost her job and her boyfriend all in one day. Now, with no new jobs on the horizon, staying on her friends couch may be more permanent than she anticipated.<br /><br />That is, until the opportunity of a lifetime falls into her lap! Stay at the Bartholomew apartment building in New York City. One of the most famous landmarks with a dark, mysterious history behind it. And…She’ll be paid twelve thousand dollars to apartment sit! <b>Seriously! How could she say no!?</b><br /><br />Ahhh, not so fast - there are rules! One of which include no guests...period! I absolutely loved <i>Final Girls</i>, but his next release <i>The Last Time I Lied</i> missed the mark for me. <br /><br />Riley Sager's newest release is an addictive thriller that is a little dark and even spooky at times. I was so caught up in the “one more chapter” mode that I kept reading beyond our buddy read goals. <br /><br />If only it would’ve stayed on the same path all the way through! ☹️ <br />The ending veered off in a direction that just didn’t seem to mesh with the theme of the first two thirds of the book. I wish I could say I came away loving it, but I didn’t. Not quite. For me, one star sadly fell away for the ending. But as always...that’s just me! <br /><br />A spooky fun buddy read with Susanne!<br /><br />Thank you to NetGalley, Penguin Group Dutton and Riley Sager for an ARC to read and review.<br /></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2779068932" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2779068932" />
    <a title="Larry H" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h"><img alt="Larry H" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577826084p2/5872506.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2779068932?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Larry H" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Larry H" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h">Larry H</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5872506-larry-h?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2779068932" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3107130315406579921">3.5 stars.<br/><br/>You know the old saying if it seems too good to be true, it probably is? Well, that's something that Jules Larsen <i>should have</i> thought of when she accepted an assignment as an apartment sitter at one of the oldest and most exclusive NYC apartment buildings, the Bartholomew.<br/><br/>Jules is between jobs and, because her relationship with her boyfriend just ended, between apartments. The Bartholomew was the setting of her favorite book from childhood, so the thought of living in those glamorous, </span>
  <span id="freeText3107130315406579921" style="display:none">3.5 stars.<br /><br />You know the old saying if it seems too good to be true, it probably is? Well, that's something that Jules Larsen <i>should have</i> thought of when she accepted an assignment as an apartment sitter at one of the oldest and most exclusive NYC apartment buildings, the Bartholomew.<br /><br />Jules is between jobs and, because her relationship with her boyfriend just ended, between apartments. The Bartholomew was the setting of her favorite book from childhood, so the thought of living in those glamorous, hallowed halls almost seems like a dream. When she sees the enormous, duplex apartment at the top of the building, and learns that she'll receive a salary of $4,000 for each month of her three-month assignment, how could she resist?<br /><br />Sure, there are a lot of rules. She must sleep in her apartment every night. She can't have anyone over to visit because the residents of the Bartholomew cherish their privacy. No pictures of anything related to the building on social media. She's also not allowed to bother any of the residents.<br /><br />But even those and other slightly strange rules are enough to dissuade her, given how desperately she needs the money. Even as she starts to learn about the Bartholomew's somewhat-scandalous and creepy past, she feels lucky. When she meets fellow apartment sitter Ingrid, she feels she has found a kindred spirit. As Ingrid shares her feelings about how things about the building frighten her a bit, Jules tries to help assuage her fears (and perhaps calm some of her own).<br /><br />The next morning, Ingrid is gone. She apparently left the Bartholomew without a word to anyone, and she won't return Jules' texts or phone calls. Little by little, Jules starts to become more worried about Ingrid's safety, and wonders if perhaps there is more to the things Ingrid was afraid of. As Jules tries to dig into Ingrid's disappearance with the help of her handsome neighbor, she starts to discover that things in the Bartholomew aren't as idyllic as they seem—and Ingrid isn't the first one to disappear.<br /><br />Riley Sager knows how to ratchet up the suspense, and he definitely did so here in <b>
  <i>Lock Every Door</i>
</b>. There is such a pervasive sense of danger permeating through the book from the minute Jules first arrives at the Bartholomew. You know it's too good to be true, you know she shouldn't trust people, but as the reader, you're powerless to shake some sense into her.<br /><br />The narration shifts between the present and Jules' arrival at the building a few days earlier, so you get glimpses of what will happen but nothing too concrete to fully give it away. Sager's storytelling is taut and reads like a movie, so I could picture what was happening in my mind's eye.<br /><br />You'll really need to suspend your disbelief here as the book hurtles toward its conclusion. I'll admit I thought things went completely off the rails and I rolled my eyes toward the end. But I know many others loved this book, so perhaps I just thought things got a little too kooky for my own good.<br /><br />I'm a fan of Sager's writing—his debut novel, <b>
  <i>Final Girls</i>
</b>, was another book that read like a movie I'd totally see. If you like your thrillers on the crazy, slightly gothic side, <b>
  <i>Lock Every Door</i>
</b> is one for you. And don't accept an apartment-sitting gig that seems too good to be true! <br /><br />NetGalley and PENGUIN GROUP Dutton provided me an advance copy of the book in exchange for an unbiased review. Thanks for making this available!<br /><br />See all of my reviews at <a href="http://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com</a>.<br /><br />Check out my list of the best books I read in 2018 at <a href="https://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2019/01/the-best-books-i-read-in-2018.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">https://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2019/01/the-best-books-i-read-in-2018.html</a>. <br /><br />You can follow me on Instagram at <a href="https://www.instagram.com/yrralh/" target="”_blank”" rel="nofollow noopener"> https://www.instagram.com/yrralh/.</a></span>
